# November 13, 2024 Batch Grouping

It is necessary to consider supporting the one-hot output of MIMOIIR and then calculate the frequency response.

After independently outputting each channel of MIMOIIR, it was indeed found that there is an issue:

![image-20241113103449533](assets/image-20241113103449533.png)

Not using the Sequential model and directly outputting with layers is correct:

![image-20241113110933024](assets/image-20241113110933024.png)

However, the speed is very slow. Attempting to increase the batch_size for further testing.

![image-20241113110953885](assets/image-20241113110953885.png)

Using the Sequential model is also correct and faster:

![image-20241113112258877](assets/image-20241113112258877.png)

![image-20241113112347301](assets/image-20241113112347301.png)

Here, x is reshaped to (1, -1, 1).

The structure of (1, -1) might imply that the RNN sequence has only one input value.

The Hammerstein model, due to the IIR section being placed later, is difficult to calculate in advance, resulting in poor training efficiency. It is impossible to achieve truly fast calculations.

After modifying the IIR section, a MAE of 0.0180 (sequential) and 0.0436 (random) was achieved.

It can be seen that the MAE for the sequential order has significantly improved after the IIR correction.

![image-20241113123354528](C:\Users\lyon\AppData\Roaming\Typora\typora-user-images\image-20241113123354528.png)

To speed up training, the data can be grouped by sweep points, divided into 70 groups, effectively speeding up by 70 times.

After grouping, the training speed has significantly improved.

Previously, it was incorrectly divided into 280,000 groups, resulting in only one data point per group. The RNN only calculated once, outputting a fixed ratio value to the input, which explains the issue.

![image-20241113124846387](assets/image-20241113124846387.png)

![image-20241113124855434](assets/image-20241113124855434.png)

![image-20241113125332728](assets/image-20241113125332728.png)

![image-20241113125357540](assets/image-20241113125357540.png)

Although the high frequency is slightly off, it is indeed clustering around 0.2, indicating that the relative transfer function is effective.

Using multiple features, targeting the middle, opening sample weights, softplus - 2:

![image-20241113130437878](assets/image-20241113130437878.png)

![image-20241113130447555](assets/image-20241113130447555.png)

Now it is observed that when the magnitude is small, it drifts. It may still be necessary to check the calculation method of the sample weights.

## Model Manager

**Application Background**

In the fields of machine learning and deep learning, the development, training, and management of models are becoming increasingly complex. As model sizes and training data grow, effectively managing training configurations, log histories, model weights, and other data becomes a critical issue. Existing tools may not meet the needs for multi-parameter batch training, model version management, training process tracking, and result reproducibility. Therefore, a comprehensive system is needed to manage these elements and improve the efficiency of model development and deployment.

**Functional Description**

This system aims to provide a complete model management platform with the following features:

- **Training Configuration Management**: Save and manage different training configurations, supporting multi-stage configurations and parameter batch training.
- **Model Manager**: Manage model configurations, weights, training histories, etc., supporting label filtering and weight migration between models.
- **Training Process Tracking**: Record training logs, historical optimal weights, loss values, etc., supporting continued training.
- **Inference Metric Calculation**: Support model inference and calculation of related metrics.
- **Web UI Interface**: Provide a user-friendly interface for easy operation and viewing of training results.
- **Backend Service**: Use a Python containerized backend, provide web interfaces, support starting training via JSON configuration, and return training results via HTTP protocol.

**Software Architecture**

1. **Frontend (Web UI)**:
   - Built using modern web technologies (such as React, Vue.js), providing an intuitive user interface.
   - Implement model management, configuration management, training monitoring, and other functions.

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-94.md

2. **Backend Service**:
   - Based on Python, using frameworks such as FastAPI or Django.
   - Containerized deployment, providing RESTful API interfaces.
   - Responsible for receiving training configurations, initiating training tasks, and returning training results.
3. **Model Manager Backend**:
   - Acts as a Docker launcher, which may not run inside Docker.
   - Capable of reading files inside Docker, managing model weights and training logs.
   - Provides ID allocation services to ensure the uniqueness of all elements in the system.
4. **Database**:
   - Utilizes relational databases (e.g., PostgreSQL) or NoSQL databases (e.g., MongoDB) to store configurations, models, weights, training records, etc.
   - Uses unique IDs to connect various entities, forming a network structure for easy data retrieval and reproduction.
5. **Containerized Training Environment**:
   - Uses Docker to containerize the training environment, ensuring consistency and reproducibility.
   - The backend initiates Docker containers for training by passing JSON configurations.

**Tech Stack**

- **Frontend**: HTML, CSS, JavaScript, React, or Vue.js.
- **Backend**: Python, FastAPI or Django, Docker.
- **Database**: PostgreSQL, MongoDB.
- **Containerization**: Docker, Docker Compose.
- **Others**: Redis (for caching and task queues), Celery (task scheduling), Nginx (reverse proxy).

**Optimization Plan and Supplements**

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-96.md

1. **ID Allocation and Management**:
   - Use UUID to ensure the uniqueness of each entity and avoid ID conflicts.
   - Set unique constraints in the database to prevent duplicate insertions.
2. **Multi-stage Configuration Handling**:
   - Add support for multi-stage training in the configuration, such as pre-training, fine-tuning, etc.
   - Use nested or reference mechanisms in the configuration to clearly represent parameters for different stages.
3. **Weight Management**:
   - Weights should explicitly belong to one model but allow migration between compatible models.
   - Record the source and training history in the metadata of weights for easy traceability.
4. **Security and Access Control**:
   - Pay attention to permissions and security when reading files inside Docker to prevent sensitive information leakage.
   - Implement user authentication and authorization mechanisms to protect system resources.
5. **Large File Transfer and Storage**:
   - Use object storage services (e.g., AWS S3, MinIO) to manage model weights and large log files.
   - Avoid directly transferring large files via HTTP; use pre-signed URLs or chunked upload/download instead.
6. **System Scalability and Performance**:
   - Use message queues (e.g., RabbitMQ) and task schedulers (e.g., Celery) to handle training tasks and improve system throughput.
   - Separate frontend and backend to support multiple users operating simultaneously.
7. **Logging and Monitoring**:
   - Implement a comprehensive logging mechanism to facilitate troubleshooting and performance optimization.
   - Use monitoring tools (e.g., Prometheus, Grafana) to monitor system status in real-time.
8. **Reproducibility Assurance**:
   - Save all training-related configurations, environments, and data versions to ensure the training process can be fully reproduced.
   - Record environmental information (e.g., dependency versions, hardware configurations) in the metadata of models and weights.
9. **User Experience Enhancement**:
   - Provide a user-friendly frontend interface with clear operation flows and detailed documentation and help information.
   - Support visualization of results, such as loss curves and metric changes.
10. **Continuous Integration and Deployment (CI/CD)**:
    - Use tools (e.g., Jenkins, GitLab CI/CD) to achieve continuous integration and deployment of code, ensuring system stability and update efficiency.

**Conclusion**

Through the above analysis and optimization solutions, a comprehensive model management system has been designed to meet the needs of managing training configurations, log history, weights, and more. The system adopts a web interface and containerized backend, leveraging modern technology stacks to support batch training, continued training, metric calculation, and other functions. Key data structures are connected by unique IDs, forming a network structure that ensures data integrity and reproducibility. By addressing blind spots and optimizing solutions, the system has been enhanced in terms of security, scalability, and user experience, providing strong support for the development and management of machine learning models.

Attempting to make `power_log_mae` support multiple batches, then retraining 1/2 IIR.

``` python
def power_log_mae_loss(y_true, y_pred, k=0.2, use_balence=True):
    # shape: (batch_size, simple_num, feature_num)
    # Calculate the energy for y_true and y_pred separately
    # k is the weight for the energy loss
    # Energy calculation should be done in groups of simple_num; crossing sample_num is incorrect
    # Energy shape: (batch_size, feature_num)
    power_true = tf.reduce_sum(tf.abs(y_true), axis=1)
    power_pred = tf.reduce_sum(tf.abs(y_pred), axis=1)
    
    # Take the logarithm of the energy to ensure symmetry in overestimation and underestimation
    # Logarithm does not require normalization as it inherently includes a division operation
    # Logarithm of energy shape: (batch_size, feature_num)
    power_true_log = tf.math.log(power_true + 1e-8)
    power_pred_log = tf.math.log(power_pred + 1e-8)
    
    # Calculate the mean squared error of the logarithm of energy
    loss_power_log = tf.abs(power_true_log - power_pred_log)
    
    # MAE shape: (batch_size, feature_num)
    # MAE should also be calculated in groups of simple_num to ensure correct energy normalization
    loss_mae = tf.reduce_mean(tf.abs(y_true - y_pred), axis=1)
    if use_balence:
        # When normalizing MAE, ensure it is done in groups of simple_num, corresponding one-to-one
        loss_mae = loss_mae / (power_true + 1e-8) * 350
        # Add an adjustment factor to make the balance_loss and power_log_loss of similar magnitude
    
    # Finally, average and sum to get the final loss
    loss_power_log_avr = tf.reduce_mean(loss_power_log)
    loss_mae_avr = tf.reduce_mean(loss_mae)
    
    return k * loss_power_log_avr + (1 - k) * loss_mae_avr
```

Batch size = 182 (full sweep)

There seems to be an issue that requires further inspection.

The time-domain waveform appears to be fine.

![image-20241119153524937](assets/image-20241119153524937.png)

While reviewing the data, I noticed that some data quality was poor, likely due to the fade-out at the end causing the signal amplitude to be too small. Then, when performing the FFT, only the latter part of the data was截取ed.

Therefore, the data should not be faded out, only faded in. Previously, the fade-out was applied because multiple groups of data were mistakenly combined, causing mutual interference.

Cancel the fade_out and rerun the code.

After running, the effect is basically fine:

![image-20241119155944553](assets/image-20241119155944553.png)

However, there still seems to be some issues. The output in the last segment is decreasing, with an abnormal突变.

![image-20241119160246337](assets/image-20241119160246337.png)

It should be that the filtering caused an anomaly in the last cycle, possibly because the filtering performed an FFT.

![image-20241119162044685](assets/image-20241119162044685.png)

The filtering has affected both the beginning and the end.

![image-20241119162253223](assets/image-20241119162253223.png)

Process double the data in advance and only take the middle half to avoid the impact of the beginning and end data.

This basically solves the issue at the end:

# November 22, 2024

# Design Ideas for Neural Network Models

## 1. Target System Feature Analysis

The electrochemical seismometer (MET) exhibits significant nonlinear frequency response characteristics, including:
1. Presence of notable nonlinear behavior.
2. Nonlinear characteristics are closely related to the amplitude of the input signal.
3. Within a specific magnitude range, the system exhibits quasi-linear characteristics close to linearity.

These characteristics indicate that MET is an amplitude-dependent quasi-linear system. Therefore, the new model needs to:
- Ensure effective capture of the system's quasi-linearity.
- Be able to simulate changes in the resonant peaks of the frequency response curve.
- Be able to capture the drift behavior of the center frequency of the frequency response.

## 2. Analysis of Traditional Nonlinear Models

### 2.1 Hammerstein Model
- **Features**: Combines a nonlinear stage (input stage) with a linear transfer stage. The nonlinear part processes the input signal amplitude, while the linear part handles frequency characteristics.
- **Advantages**: Can effectively simulate amplitude-dependent nonlinear characteristics.
- **Disadvantages**: In complex frequency response systems, the nonlinear effects across the entire frequency band may limit its accuracy.

### 2.2 Wiener Model
- **Features**: Combines a linear stage (input stage) with a nonlinear stage (output stage). The linear part describes the frequency response, while the nonlinear part handles amplitude dependency.
- **Advantages**: Better modeling of nonlinear characteristics at resonant frequencies compared to the Hammerstein model.
- **Disadvantages**: Unable to capture the dynamic behavior of system center frequency drift.

### 2.3 Duffing Oscillator Model
- **Features**: Based on nonlinear dynamics, describes the resonant behavior and amplitude-frequency dependency of the system.
- **Advantages**: Can simulate specific nonlinear behaviors, such as drift in resonant frequency.
- **Disadvantages**: Difficult to extend in complex frequency response systems, limited to specific frequency variations.

## 3. Selecting the Wiener Model and Designing a Combined System Model

Among the traditional models mentioned above, the Wiener model offers better flexibility and modeling capabilities for resonant nonlinear characteristics. Therefore, a combined system model based on the Wiener model is proposed:

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-108.md

- **Design Concept**: Treat the linear and nonlinear parts of the system as independent sub-models.
- **Implementation Goal**: Simultaneously model the linear and nonlinear characteristics of the system.

Experimental results show that the combined model can effectively capture the nonlinearity of the resonant frequency of MET, but there are still limitations:
- **Limitations**: It cannot accurately capture the dynamic characteristics of the system's center frequency drift.

## 4. Model Enhancement and Neural Network Design

### 4.1 Neural Network Integration
To address the shortcomings in modeling the center frequency drift, the combined model was redesigned with neural network integration:
1. Use neural networks to enhance the model's nonlinear expressive capabilities.
2. Convert the linear and nonlinear components into trainable modules of the neural network.

### 4.2 Nonlinear Dimension Expansion
On the basis of neural network integration, further expand the nonlinear dimension:
- **Method**: Introduce piecewise nonlinear activation functions.
- **Effect**: Enhance the model's ability to capture complex nonlinear characteristics.

### 4.3 Final Design: IIR-LNRNN Model
Combining the capabilities of IIR convolution cores and neural networks, design a hybrid model of linear and nonlinear components:
- **Model Structure**:
  - **IIR Convolution Core**: Simulates the linear dynamic behavior of the system.
  - **Piecewise Nonlinear Activation Function**: Captures complex nonlinear characteristics.
  - **Neural Network Structure**: Learns dynamic characteristics across different frequency ranges.
- **Advantages**:
  1. Simultaneously models linear and nonlinear characteristics.
  2. Effectively models the center frequency drift and resonant peak variations of MET.
  3. Improves the model's generalization ability for dynamic nonlinear characteristics.

## 5. Experimental Validation

Experimental results show that the IIR-LNRNN model has significant advantages over traditional models in the following aspects:
1. **Dynamic Linearity**: Effectively reduces amplitude-frequency distortion caused by system nonlinearity.
2. **Frequency Response Stability**: Accurately captures the dynamic changes in frequency drift and resonant peaks.
3. **Computational Efficiency**: The model design combines IIR convolution kernels and neural networks, making it suitable for real-time processing in embedded systems.

In summary, the IIR-LNRNN model provides an efficient and precise solution for the nonlinear modeling of MET, while also offering new modeling ideas for other nonlinear systems with complex dynamic characteristics.

# Missing Content:

2. Mathematical derivation of the relationship between energy loss and frequency response drift.

5. Missing comparative experiments, such as comparisons with traditional single-proportion linearity calibration, Wiener, and Hammerstein-type nonlinear compensation effects.

6. Missing comparison of dynamic linearity values. Consider dynamic linearity as a frequency-varying curve and define an overall dynamic linearity metric (maximum or average).

![image-20241214195339725](assets/image-20241214195339725.png)

![image-20241214195112282](assets/image-20241214195112282.png)

To avoid the input layer being overly affected by dropout, consider increasing the number of parameters in the input layer, trying h8u6l6. h8*0.8≈h6, which might help restore the performance to the level of h6u6l6.

Based on the analysis, consider adding a dropout in the middle of the network.

> ### Analysis of the Impact of Introducing Dropout at Different Positions
>
> 1. **Adding Dropout at the Input Layer**
>
>    - **Mechanism**: Randomly discards input features, equivalent to a special form of data augmentation for the input data.

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-113.md

>    - Effects
>
>      :
>
>      - Helps the model avoid over-reliance on certain input features, thereby improving generalization ability.
>      - May also make the model harder to converge in the early stages of training, as the "effective features" seen by the model are constantly changing.
>
>    - **Impact on Features**: Causes the most disturbance to the initial feature representation of the model, i.e., increases uncertainty from the very beginning of training.
>
> 2. **Adding Dropout in the Middle Layers (Hidden Layers)**
>
>    - **Mechanism**: Randomly drops the activation values of neurons in the hidden layers to prevent co-adaptation of internal feature representations within the network.
>
>    - Effects
>
>      :
>
>      - The most common and widely used approach.
>      - Adds randomness to the intermediate representations of the network, guiding the network to learn more robust and redundant-free features.
>      - Generally has a relatively balanced impact on the overall structure of the network, neither excessively disrupting the model's initial extraction of input features nor directly perturbing the decision values of the final output layer.
>
>    - **Impact on Features**: Affects features between the input and output. The model has already preliminarily extracted low-level features, and applying Dropout at this stage helps strengthen the robustness of the features. The impact on training stability is relatively controllable.
>
> 3. **Adding Dropout Before the Output Layer (Before the Output Layer)**
>
>    - **Mechanism**: Drops features before the final decision layer (e.g., fully connected layer or classification layer).
>
>    - Effects
>
>      :
>
>      - Directly affects the final decision signal of the model, which can have a relatively significant impact on the model's stability.
>      - If excessive Dropout causes severe damage to the feature representation before the output layer, it may reduce the model's prediction accuracy and consistency.
>
>    - **Impact on Features**: Perturbs the final decision signal, potentially making it harder for the model to converge during training or causing significant fluctuations in the output probability distribution.
>
> ### Analyzing Dropout Placement Based on Impact
>
> - **Most Impactful Cases**:
>   Generally, adding Dropout **before the input layer or output layer** has a more direct and noticeable impact on model performance.
>   - Input layer Dropout perturbs the original data features, forcing the model to train with "missing features" to a large extent, which can sometimes make early training unstable.
>   - Dropout before the output layer directly affects the stability of the final decision. If not carefully set in the later stages of training, it can lead to significant fluctuations in prediction results.
> - **Less Impactful and More Commonly Used Cases**:
>   Adding Dropout in the **middle hidden layers** is usually a relatively moderate approach. This method neither excessively alters the initial distribution of input features nor overly perturbs the final output decision.

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-114.md

> Therefore, applying Dropout to intermediate layers achieves the purpose of conventional regularization without introducing excessive instability during the initial training phase or final decision-making. This is also the most common and mature practice for applying Dropout in deep learning models.
>
> ### Summary
>
> - **Minimal Impact**: Dropout in intermediate layers (hidden layers) has a moderate impact on model structure and performance, and is typically the best practice.
> - **Significant Impact**: Dropout before the input layer or output layer can cause significant interference during the initial training phase (input layer) or the later decision-making phase (output layer), and thus requires careful handling and fine-tuning.

FRIKANh8u6l6 adds dropout to the input layer

![image-20241214201134850](assets/image-20241214201134850.png)

``` python
    def build_kan_inner_layers(self, iir_out):
        # Directly connect the inner layers of KAN
        x = iir_out
        # for kan_inner in self.kan_inner_layers:
        #     x = kan_inner(x)
        for i, kan_inner in enumerate(self.kan_inner_layers):
            x = kan_inner(x)
            if i == len(self.kan_inner_layers) // 2:
                if self.dropout_layer is not None and self.dropout_position == 'inner':
                    # Add dropout in the middle layer
                    x = self.dropout_layer(x)
        return x
```

# December 15, 2024

It is possible to directly build_LUT for KAN.

1. Implement kan_for in Python.
2. Implement kan_lut in Python.
3. Implement kan_for in C.
4. Implement kan_lut in C.

bshape also requires multiplication and addition, which involves the control points (weights) and basis functions. After multiplication and addition, a bshape function y_b(x) can be obtained. Quantization can be applied to either the basis functions or the weighted basis functions.

![6e7546bd727d422bc9301b1d86e866ce](assets/6e7546bd727d422bc9301b1d86e866ce.jpg)

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-122.md

![image-20241217223038420](assets/image-20241217223038420.png)

The decimal precision has been changed to 12 digits, and it seems that there might indeed be an issue with float.

![image-20241218095006479](assets/image-20241218095006479.png)

Fixed the internal issue with IIR, and the correct result was calculated using double.

![image-20241218100344187](assets/image-20241218100344187.png)

![image-20241218100444789](assets/image-20241218100444789.png)

The correct result was also calculated using float, so we can continue using float.

```c
static inline port_float fabsf(port_float x) {
    union {
        port_float f;
        uint32_t u;
    } tmp;
    tmp.f = x;
    tmp.u &= 0x7FFFFFFF;  // Clear the sign bit
    return tmp.f;
}
```

The implementation of fabsf corresponds to float. If it were switched to double, issues would arise.

# December 23, 2024

>Below is an **academic review** and evaluation of the paper based on the high standards and requirements of **SCI Zone 1 journal review**, provided for the author's reference and improvement.
>
>------
>
>## I. Research Background and Innovation
>
>1. **Importance of the Topic**
>   - The paper focuses on the nonlinear compensation problem of electrochemical seismometers (MET) and aims to achieve real-time correction on resource-constrained embedded platforms.
>   - In fields such as geophysics and seismic monitoring, high-sensitivity and broadband seismometers are of great significance for earthquake early warning and disaster prevention, and there is an urgent need for nonlinear compensation of sensors.
>   - The topic has practical application value and scientific research significance, representing a key issue in the field of seismic observation instruments.
>2. **Innovation**
>   - The paper proposes a neural network (FRIKAN) that integrates the Kolmogorov–Arnold (KA) theorem with frequency response information, introduces a trainable B-spline activation function with physical constraints, and combines FRIRNN (RNN based on IIR filter parameters) to inject frequency response priors, forming a physically interpretable network structure.
>   - The application of a lookup table (LUT) to accelerate KAN inference and the performance comparison experiments on embedded platforms are relatively novel.
>   - Compared to traditional "black-box" networks like LSTM/GRU, the authors attempt to optimize with physical quantities such as frequency response, sensitivity, and inherent frequency drift as core objectives. This "frequency response loss function" approach is inspiring for sensor nonlinear compensation.
>
>Overall, the paper presents some valuable ideas on the deep integration of physical knowledge and neural networks, demonstrating a certain level of **originality**.
>
>------
>
>## II. Technical Methods and Theoretical Completeness
>
>1. **Derivation and Physical Interpretation of FRIRNN**
>   - The derivation process of equivalently converting IIR filters into state space and RNN is clear, explaining how to inject linear frequency response physical priors into a trainable RNN.
>   - The paper constructs a parallel FRIRNN core array for each amplitude in the case of multiple magnitudes (snapshots); this design is mathematically feasible and can retain frequency response priors for different amplitudes.
>   - It is recommended to more explicitly discuss the potential impact of **parallel multi-snapshot FRIRNN** on network parameter scale and stability, and to explain how the snapshot strategy handles interpolation or transition mechanisms in real-world continuous data, to further enhance the method's explanatory power and universality.

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-124.md

>2. **KAN Spline Activation Function and Physical Constraints**
>   - The paper points out the application of B-spline functions to directly learn the nonlinear calibration curves of sensors and proposes physical laws and prior knowledge such as odd symmetry and co-directional constraints.
>   - Spline curves often have excellent fitting capabilities and controllability for nonlinear mappings, but they may also lead to issues such as local overfitting and excessive jitter. It is recommended to supplement the explanation of how to select the number of segments (number of knots) or the order in practical implementations, as well as how to prevent overfitting (e.g., regularization), to help readers better understand its stability and generalization ability.
>   - Physical interpretability is one of the highlights of this paper, but it is suggested that the authors further provide some qualitative or quantitative examples in the text to demonstrate the shape of the B-spline curve learned after the activation function training and how it corresponds to the MET nonlinear calibration curve.
>3. **Frequency Response Loss Function Design**
>   - The paper proposes the Amplitude Frequency MAE (AFMAE) to measure the amplitude error of the output sine wave and combines it with conventional time-domain loss to obtain a joint loss that considers both time and frequency domains.
>   - This approach indeed has reference value in fields such as nonlinear sensor compensation and broadband amplitude retention, but it has only been tested in the scenario of swept sine waves. It remains unclear whether the same effect can be maintained with more complex actual seismic waveforms or random inputs.
>   - It is recommended to supplement the article with test results on more complex excitations such as random or real seismic data to prove the generalizability and applicability of AFMAE in actual signal scenarios, thereby enhancing persuasiveness.
>
>------
>
>## III. Experimental Design and Result Analysis
>
>1. **Dataset and Experimental Coverage**
>   - The authors obtained multi-frequency and multi-amplitude swept data based on a vibration test bench to construct the training and test sets. This process can verify effectiveness in a laboratory environment, but there may still be a gap from real seismic conditions.
>   - It is recommended that the authors supplement the explanation:
>     1. Whether the sweep range, frequency point density, and maximum excitation amplitude during testing are sufficiently close to the actual seismic environment?
>     2. How does it perform under certain changes in conditions such as noise, temperature, and aging?
>     3. If possible, further comparison with seismic record waveforms (real/simulated) would be more convincing.
>2. **Comparative Experiment Design**
>   - The paper compares LSTM, GRU, RNN, and Wiener, controlling roughly similar parameter scales, and examines indicators such as nonlinearity and sensitivity drift. The overall comparison dimensions are quite comprehensive.
>   - In terms of chart presentation, the comparison of nonlinear residuals and model parameter quantities has been provided, demonstrating the potential of FRIKAN in balancing "high performance-low parameters."

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-125.md

>   - It is recommended that the authors provide **more detailed statistical analysis** in the comparative experiments: such as presenting the average results and variance of training under multiple random initial conditions, or further validating with independent datasets, as well as the trade-offs between time-domain and frequency-domain metrics under different loss weights (β), to make the robustness of the experimental results more clearly visible.
>3. **LUT Acceleration and Embedded Implementation**
>   - The authors conducted LUT-based acceleration on the STM32F405 MCU, achieving significant performance improvements compared to LSTM.
>   - It is suggested to **more explicitly quantify** in the text (1) the impact of LUT table size on SRAM, Flash, and other resources under different interpolation accuracies; (2) the speed difference between small-batch inference vs. streaming real-time inference; (3) if the number of LUT segments increases, whether there is a turning point or upper limit in accuracy and speed?
>
>------
>
>## IV. Paper Structure and Writing Quality
>
>1. **Overall Structure**
>   - The paper is written in the order of Introduction → Theoretical Derivation and System Analysis → Model Design and Implementation → Experimental Testing → Results Discussion → Conclusion, with a clear logical framework and smooth flow of thought.
>   - It is recommended to consider moving some of the more in-depth derivations and formulas to the appendix, especially parts like bilinear transformation and matrix-form derivations, to enhance the clarity of the main text.
>2. **Chart Expression**
>   - The charts are quite rich, displaying various forms such as frequency response curves, input-output curves, scatter plots, and box plots. The readability is generally good, clearly presenting nonlinear drift and compensation effects.
>   - It is suggested to further enhance the annotations on some key charts (such as the comparison of frequency response before and after compensation), including quantitative compensation effects, coordinate annotations, color/line type differentiation, corresponding frequency points or amplitude ranges, etc., to improve the readability of the charts.
>3. **Language and Details**
>   - The overall writing of the paper is fluent, with some paragraphs having high technical content, and the use of academic terminology is mostly correct.
>   - Some parts could be further condensed to reduce repetitive descriptions and overly long formulas, allowing readers to grasp the key points more quickly.
>   - It is recommended to check the unified format of the references, especially ensuring that the arrangement and citation of references comply with IEEE format requirements, and to ensure that the latest research findings are also cited (especially in international cutting-edge directions such as neural networks combined with physical information and sensor compensation).
>
>------
>
>## V. Comprehensive Evaluation and Suggestions for Future Improvements
>
>1. **Summary of Advantages**
>   - The paper proposes an innovative approach **combining physical priors with neural networks** for MET nonlinear compensation, with both interpretability and computational efficiency.
>   - The experiments systematically demonstrate the performance changes before and after compensation, as well as comparisons with traditional deep learning and classical nonlinear models, and provide LUT acceleration results on an embedded platform, showing certain practical value.
>2. **Shortcomings and Directions for Improvement**

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-126.md

>   - **Experimental Diversity**: Currently, the evaluation of frequency response compensation is mainly based on synthesized data from swept sine waves. It is possible to further incorporate real seismic signals (or complex random excitations) for assessment and quantify the actual improvements in downstream seismic detection and magnitude measurement.
>   - **Model Robustness**: Although additional learning rate strategies were employed, phenomena such as overfitting were observed in LSTM during comparative experiments. Consider increasing the experimental statistics or using data augmentation, regularization, early stopping, etc., to provide readers with a clearer understanding of the robustness differences among various methods in actual deployment.
>   - **Physical Constraints and KA Splines**: The paper demonstrates the potential of trainable B-splines in constructing physically constrained mappings, but further research on their intrinsic mechanisms, parameter sensitivity, and generalization could be enriched.
>   - **Application Porting and Large-Scale Deployment**: The current acceleration results on MCU platforms are relatively preliminary. Further quantification of key metrics such as LUT size, memory usage, and real-time processing throughput could enhance the argument for the feasibility of actual deployment.
>3. **Overall Conclusion**
>   - The paper has a high level of completion in terms of **problem selection, theoretical derivation, experimental design, and results presentation**, with novel content and experimental results that support the main conclusions.
>   - If the authors further improve in areas such as **expanding experiments**, **supplementing more real-world scenario tests**, and **deepening the discussion on stability and model scalability**, it is believed that the academic impact and engineering application potential of this work could be significantly enhanced.
>   - Given the current research results, the paper has certain publication value. It is recommended that the authors submit it to high-impact journals (such as SCI Zone 1 and top journals in related interdisciplinary fields) after revisions and improvements.
>
>------
>
>**Review Summary**:
>This study proposes a nonlinear compensation network (FRIKAN) that integrates physical priors, demonstrating interpretability, generalization, and advantages in embedded deployment for nonlinear correction in electrochemical seismometers. The overall quality is good, and it is recommended to supplement or revise the following points before publication:
>
>1. Expand data evaluation in real-world scenarios, providing more tests with complex input signals/seismic waveforms;
>2. Provide a deeper explanation of the selection of B-spline activation, regularization methods, and the stability of parallel multi-snapshot RNNs;
>3. Add discussions on different LUT parameter settings and the trade-off between accuracy and memory consumption;
>4. Further improve chart annotations and literature citation formats.
>
>If the above modifications are properly made, the persuasiveness of the paper and readers' understanding of the method's operability can be significantly enhanced, thereby increasing its influence in the field.

# December 25, 2024

>
>
>## I. Overall Evaluation and Recommendations
>
>### Comprehensive Evaluation

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-127.md

>This paper addresses the issue of nonlinear frequency response compensation for electrochemical seismometers (MET) by proposing a deep model, FRIKAN, which integrates frequency response prior information with the concept of Kolmogorov-Arnold networks (KAN). The model is validated for feasibility in embedded microcontrollers through the use of B-spline activation functions, frequency response loss functions, and a LUT-based acceleration strategy. Overall:

>- **Innovation**: The combination of KAN with frequency response prior information and its validation in nonlinear compensation scenarios, particularly for seismometers, presents a novel approach.
>- **Feasibility**: The experimental data is sufficiently comprehensive, validating the method's effectiveness through sweep frequency tests, amplitude scans, and embedded implementations, with convincing results.
>- **Structure and Readability**: The paper is well-structured, divided into introduction, background theory, model design, experiments, and conclusion, with a logical flow. The inclusion of illustrations, flowcharts, and block diagrams is relatively comprehensive.
>- **Shortcomings**: There are still some details and explanations that need refinement (such as literature citations, handling of TODO items, etc.), requiring modifications and additions. Furthermore, the paper could benefit from more quantitative or direct comparisons with existing methods or related literature.

>Given the overall research depth and experimental completeness of the paper, **this reviewer is inclined towards "major revisions with potential for acceptance"**, with specific revision suggestions as follows.

>------

>## II. Main Revision Suggestions for the Paper

>The following suggestions are based on the standards of SCI Zone 1 journals, requiring rigorous and in-depth support in both theoretical exposition and experimental validation.

>### 1. Further Clarify Comparisons with Existing Methods and Contributions

>- **Comparison Literature**: Although the paper mentions traditional or common methods such as NARMAX, Wiener models, and LSTM/GRU, the comparisons between them could be more direct. For example, the experimental section could specifically provide residual curves or numerical comparisons at typical frequency/amplitude points for each model, or introduce benchmark results from existing literature methods in the evaluation of embedded inference time (inference speed), to more intuitively display the relative advantages and disadvantages of FRIKAN.
>- **Highlighting Contributions**: Although multiple "innovative points" are listed in the introduction, it is recommended to summarize them again in the conclusion or discussion, and present them in a concise table or list format, highlighting the "gains" or "performance improvements" of FRIKAN compared to traditional models.

>### 2. Experimental Design and Data Reproducibility

>- **Division of Training and Testing Data**: The paper already lists some settings for training/validation/testing (e.g., 50%/50%), but providing more details on data balance and whether cross-validation (k-fold) was performed would be more persuasive.

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-128.md

>- **Noise and Error Analysis**: Seismic detectors often encounter noise in practical measurements. The paper mentions filtering for noise reduction, but it could add more details in the experimental section regarding noise intensity, Signal-to-Noise Ratio (SNR) comparisons, or observing residual noise in the frequency spectrum. This would help reviewers more comprehensively assess the model's robustness.
>
>### 3. Completeness of Model Structure and Formula Derivation
>
>- Frequency Response Injection and Relative Transfer Function
>
>  :
>
>  - When deriving the relative transfer function \relativeH(s)\relative{H}(s)\relativeH(s), the paper uses the ratio between the nominal transfer function of the linear system and the fitted transfer function from actual measurements. This approach is good, but it needs to emphasize whether "this is only applicable to single-input single-output systems that can be approximated as second-order systems?" If applied to more complex systems (e.g., higher-order systems or those with more coupled modes), is this method still valid? It is suggested to include a discussion on its applicability in the text.
>  - When converting to a discretized IIR using the bilinear transform, it is recommended to add a note about the inherent distortion at high frequencies (a characteristic of the bilinear transform) and how this impact is minimized in this study, such as by selecting an appropriate sampling rate or pre-envelope filtering.
>
>- KAN Spline Activation Function
>
>  :
>
>  - The introduction of the B-spline activation function is explained in the text, but it could be expanded in the "3.3 Physically Constrained KAN Spline Activation Function" section by adding references or more example curves to demonstrate how the B-spline satisfies the "odd symmetry" and "same-direction" constraints. This would help readers better understand why the B-spline is used.
>  - If space is limited, it is still suggested to add a brief paragraph explaining how the "odd symmetry" and "same-direction" constraints are specifically implemented (e.g., whether the spline nodes are symmetrically arranged or if penalty terms are added to the loss function). This would clarify the specific engineering implementation details for readers.
>
>### 4. Frequency Response MAE Loss Function and Hyperparameter Settings
>
>- Rationality of Frequency Response MAE (AFMAE)
>
>  :
>
>  - Although the formula shows that this metric focuses more on amplitude-frequency differences, the paper mentions the advantage of "avoiding overfitting to time-domain noise." Could a more specific explanation be provided? For example, compared to traditional MSE/MAE, how does AFMAE better maintain focus on overall amplitude without being overly affected by random phase perturbations when dealing with high-frequency noise in the time domain?
>
>- Loss Function Weight \wMAE \wMAE\wMAE
>
>  :
>
>  - It is recommended to provide more details about the tuning process or performance curves to convince readers that the chosen value (e.g., 0.2) is based on experimental comparisons rather than being arbitrary. Key ablation study results could be included in the appendix.
>
>### 5. Interpretability of the Parallel FRIRNN Core "Multi-Snapshot" Structure

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-129.md

>- **Handling High-Order Effects After Parallel Connection**: The paper proposes a novel and effective approach to capture nonlinearity by injecting different IIR kernels in parallel for snapshots of varying amplitudes. However, after connecting multiple FRIRNN kernels in parallel, could this lead to an excessive number of trainable parameters and inaccurate linear interpolation in the transition zone between large and small magnitudes? This could potentially be illustrated in experiments through visualization or testing the transition behavior at peak points.
>- **Scalability of Multi-Kernel Arrays**: If more amplitudes or finer magnitude sampling are encountered in the future, could this result in a rapid expansion of the number of parallel kernels? This could be briefly mentioned in the discussion section.

>### 6. References and Formatting Details
>
>- Pay attention to checking the citation format and completeness. Some places like "\hl{TODO: Why use relative transfer functions...}" or similar explanatory text can be streamlined or merged depending on the length.
>- Some citations could be more precise, such as "wangInputAmplitudeBasedAdaptive2024wangInputAmplitudeBasedAdaptive2024wangInputAmplitudeBasedAdaptive2024". Ensure that the journal or conference source, year, volume, issue, and page numbers are complete to facilitate reader retrieval.
>
>------
>
>## III. Analysis and Suggestions for Handling TODOs in the Text
>
>The "TODO" markers in the paper mostly indicate places for formula derivations, chart supplements, or illustrative diagrams. Whether these TODOs should be retained and improved is suggested as follows:
>
>1. **"TODO: Redraw the diagram"/"TODO: Redraw the block diagram" etc.**
>   - It is recommended to address all of these and avoid having "TODO" appear directly in the main text. If space is limited, consider retaining only the most critical schematic or block diagrams, with the rest placed in supplementary materials or appendices.
>   - For SCI journals, the precision and readability of charts are crucial. It is advisable to keep diagrams as clear and accurate as possible, with key parameters and their meanings explained in the captions.
>2. **"TODO: Why use relative transfer functions... Add an illustrative diagram"**
>   - This is a key TODO that helps readers understand the core idea of the paper. It is best to add an explanation in the main text or simplify it to an appropriate length. If concerned about length, detailed derivations can be placed in the appendix, but the main text should at least explain "the physical meaning of relative transfer functions" and "why directly using the ratio of measured to nominal systems simplifies compensation implementation."
>   - Given that this is one of the core ideas of the paper, it is recommended to **retain and improve** it.
>3. **"TODO: Calculate the computational load of KAN and LSTM separately... Add an interpolation diagram"**
>   - If it is possible to show the trend of KAN's multiply-accumulate operations with increasing spline segments or LUT points, it would help readers understand the model complexity and memory usage. If space is insufficient, this could be placed in the appendix or briefly summarized in a comparison table.

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-130.md

>   - If this section is not well-developed, it may give the impression that the discussion on computational complexity in the paper is not thorough enough, which could be questioned during the review process. It is recommended to **retain it appropriately**. If space is severely limited, it can be simplified to text descriptions (without extensive illustrations).
>
>In summary, the TODO items in the paper are mostly related to core formulas or experimental presentations, **it is not recommended to significantly delete them**, but rather **they should be completed or streamlined to an appropriate length before formal submission**, to avoid leaving a bad impression on the reviewers.
>
>------
>
>## IV. Are there any "fatal flaws" that could lead to rejection
>
>From the existing content, there are no obvious "fatal flaws" that would directly lead to rejection, but the following points should still be noted to prevent being questioned during external review:
>
>1. **Data Sufficiency and Representativeness**: Is it only conducted on one or a few METs? If the data source is single and the sample size is small, it may be questioned for its generalizability. Adding more actual seismic detector data or outdoor measurement scenarios would be more convincing.
>2. **Theoretical and Engineering Applicability**: Is the proposed FRIKAN only applicable to nonlinear systems dominated by "second-order approximation"? If more limitations or discussions (such as damping, number of resonance peaks, etc.) can be added in the text, it can reduce doubts about "generality" during review.
>3. **Rigor of Mathematical Derivation**: The references to bilinear transformation, KA theorem, and physical constraints on spline activation functions are relatively complete at the principle level, but it is necessary to check if there are any key steps missing references or derivation explanations.
>
>If the above issues can be appropriately supplemented and explained during revision, they will not become "fatal flaws".
>
>------
>
>## V. Are there any "minefields" that could cause reviewer反感
>
>1. **Many "TODO" items left in the paper**: If a large number of "TODO" items still appear in the submission version, or obvious blank annotations appear in the schematic diagrams, it will make the reviewers think that the paper is not yet complete.
>2. **Excessive length or redundancy**: If not appropriately streamlined at the time of submission, resulting in a significantly over-length paper, it will create a reading burden for the reviewers.
>3. **Non-standard citations**: For example, a large number of self-citations or extensive citations of non-formal materials (such as unpublished versions on arXiv) without sufficient citations of peer-reviewed papers can easily raise questions.
>
>Avoiding the above situations will basically not leave a significant negative impression.
>
>------
>
>## VI. Recommended Conclusion
>
>In summary:
>
>- **Paper Topic**: It has certain academic and application value, belonging to a relatively new method exploration.
>- **Innovation and Contribution**: The neural network structure based on fused physical priors (FRIKAN) indeed has highlights in nonlinear compensation scenarios; the experimental part is also relatively complete.
>- **Existing Issues**: More comprehensive explanations are needed for literature comparison, algorithm details, experimental reproducibility, etc., and the remaining TODO content in the paper should be handled properly.
>
>**Recommended Conclusion: Major Revision**.

![image-20250102105810793](assets/image-20250102105810793.png)

The results were reproduced on a cloud-based 2080TI, with no difference in validation loss, though there were slight numerical differences in decimal points.

![image-20250102110113641](assets/image-20250102110113641.png)

![image-20250102110547700](assets/image-20250102110547700.png)

The issue has been largely identified: there is a difference in floating-point precision between the 20-series and 30-series GPUs. The next step is to consider disabling TF32 on the 30-series and compare the results.

Disabling TF32 on the 3090:

```python
    tf.config.experimental.enable_tensor_float_32_execution(False)
    print("TF32 enabled:", tf.config.experimental.tensor_float_32_execution_enabled())
```

![image-20250102130921227](assets/image-20250102130921227.png)

![image-20250102131009736](assets/image-20250102131009736.png)

The mystery is solved: the precision loss is indeed caused by TF32. Therefore, in future training and evaluation, it is essential to ensure that TF32 is disabled.

Performance comparison:

![image-20250102131437667](assets/image-20250102131437667.png)

![image-20250102131950846](assets/image-20250102131950846.png)

Enabling TF32 actually slows down the process, not only reducing precision but also increasing time. TF32 should not be enabled.

![3.90](assets/image-20250102132843647.png)

The price for 2080TI is 1.18 yuan/hour, while the 3090 is 1.58 yuan/hour.

Training once on the 2080TI costs 10.62 yuan for 9 hours, while on the 3090 it costs 11.06 yuan for 7 hours. The costs are similar, so either the 3090 or 2080TI can be used, as long as TF32 is not enabled.

TF32 essentially reduces 32-bit precision to 16-bit precision.

![image-20250109114259142](assets/image-20250109114259142.png)

Compensation curve plotting results, the issue is fluctuations at low magnitudes, consider reducing the spline order (currently 3).

![image-20250109114653183](assets/image-20250109114653183.png)

![image-20250109114927332](assets/image-20250109114927332.png)

The problem still exists, consider not placing overly detailed breakpoints.

It might be due to insufficient training data at low magnitudes, but starting from 0.5 would degrade the performance (originally 1.0~5.0).

![image-20250109115805339](assets/image-20250109115805339.png)

Less than 0.5 would directly cause loss inf, making training impossible.

First train with 1.0~5.0, then perform breakpoint training with 0.1~5.0.

![image-20250109120413369](assets/image-20250109120413369.png)

It can be seen that the training effect is still limited.

For simple models, MAE might be better.

![image-20250109120711235](assets/image-20250109120711235.png)

Training MAE from scratch, using MAE indeed performs better, stability issues no longer occur, only minor fluctuations remain (second order).

![image-20250109120926879](assets/image-20250109120926879.png)

![image-20250109121138995](assets/image-20250109121138995.png)

Avoid plotting data with absolute values less than 0.2.

Consider plotting again.

# January 16, 2025 Added LUT Memory Usage and MAE Diagram

![image-20250116004018558](assets/image-20250116004018558.png)

>
>
>The following are the simulated review comments and suggestions for this manuscript based on the IEEE Transactions on Industrial Electronics (TIE, SCI Q1). The review comments include: overall evaluation of the manuscript, recommendation (reject/major revision/minor revision/accept), detailed reasons for required modifications or additions (listed in order of severity), and a conclusion on whether there are any structural fatal flaws. For the authors' reference.
>
>------
>
>## I. Overall Evaluation
>
>This paper addresses the nonlinear frequency response compensation problem of electrochemical seismometers (MET) by proposing a neural network (FRIKAN) that integrates frequency response information with the Kolmogorov–Arnold (KA) theorem. The paper's approach is somewhat innovative, particularly in combining the important physical prior information of frequency response with the trainable structure of spline activation functions to reduce overfitting and poor interpretability caused by the "black box" nature of traditional deep learning. The paper also invests considerable effort in experimental design and validation, including building a multi-frequency and multi-magnitude dataset, defining a frequency-domain loss function, and inference acceleration on embedded platforms, demonstrating a good overall experimental system.
>
>In terms of TIE standards, the topic of the paper—nonlinear compensation for sensors/measurement and control devices—and its embedded implementation have significant application value in the field of industrial electronics and sensors. This work aligns well with TIE's focus on high-performance sensor signal processing, smart manufacturing, and industrial embedded systems. Overall, the paper has the potential to proceed to the next round of review or final acceptance. However, there are still some issues that need further refinement and clarification. Detailed comments are provided below, listed in order of severity.
>
>------
>
>## II. Review Recommendations
>
>### Recommendation: **Major Revision**
>
>Overall, the paper does not warrant "rejection" as the innovative points, methodology, and experimental validation framework all demonstrate good research value and fit well within the scope of industrial electronics journals. However, significant revisions and additions are needed in areas such as experimental reproducibility, depth of comparison with existing literature, detailed discussion of network structure and application scenarios, and writing organization. If the authors can effectively address the review comments and make systematic revisions, there is a high likelihood of acceptance.
>
>Additionally, the paper **does not** exhibit any particularly obvious "structural/directional fatal flaws" (e.g., research direction severely misaligned with the journal's theme, overall methodology being incorrect or invalid, substantive data or algorithmic fraud, etc.). The current issues mainly lie in insufficient argumentation and writing, which require careful revision.
>
>------
>
>## III. Detailed Reasons for Required Modifications and Additions (Listed from Most to Least Severe)

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-142.md

> The following issues are listed in order of severity, from the most critical (most urgently needing resolution) to relatively minor ones.
>
>1. **Insufficient Experimental Reproducibility and Lack of Key Parameter Disclosure (Most Severe)**
>
>   - **Issue Manifestation**
>
>     : Although some experimental parameters (such as sampling frequency, number of measurement points, learning rate strategy, etc.) are listed in the text, many implementation details are still missing. For example:
>
>     1. Can more key implementation details or pseudocode be disclosed for the hyperparameters, trainable coefficient ranges, and initialization methods of the proposed FRIRNN kernel array layer and KAN spline activation function?
>     2. The detailed process of implementing the LUT acceleration strategy on embedded systems, as well as the trade-offs between lookup table accuracy and memory usage, are still insufficiently described (only a brief trend is shown in the figure).
>
>   - **Suggestion**: Supplement more details on reproducibility experiments, including network structure hyperparameters (hidden layer dimensions, number of spline nodes, training step size, etc.), and provide reproducible training/testing scripts in the appendix or through a public code link to facilitate replication by other researchers in the field.
>
>2. **Insufficient Comparison and Depth of Discussion with Existing Literature and Mainstream Methods**
>
>   - **Issue Manifestation**
>
>     : Although Section 2 and Section 3 briefly review other nonlinear compensation methods (such as Wiener/NARMAX/Volterra, PINNs, and some variants of digital predistortion), the differences and advantages of the proposed FRIKAN are not fully elaborated. For example:
>
>     1. Can Wiener models or Volterra series also incorporate certain physical priors? Is there a more detailed quantitative comparison of the training cost, model complexity, and effectiveness between them and FRIKAN?
>     2. What is the core mathematical difference between FRIKAN and PINNs/"physics-inspired" networks?
>
>   - **Suggestion**: Strengthen the comparison of advantages and disadvantages with existing methods in the literature review and experimental comparison. It would be best to demonstrate the superior performance, complexity, memory usage, and training time of FRIKAN through quantitative comparison experiments (such as modeling on the same dataset or comparing under the same parameter conditions).
>
>3. **Necessity of Industrial Application or Larger-Scale Experimental Validation**
>
>   - **Issue Manifestation**: The current experiments mainly focus on a single or limited type of MET sensor. Can this method demonstrate universality for a wider range of seismic sensors (or other industrial vibration measurement devices)? Although the article mentions that "this method can be extended to other nonlinear sensors," it lacks broader testing evidence or application examples in industrial scenarios.
>   - **Suggestion**: If space permits, it is recommended to add further scenario testing results or elaborate more on the transferability of the proposed method to other industrial measurement tasks in the discussion section (e.g., how to quickly deploy the calibration process to different sensors, whether a large amount of recalibration data is needed, etc.).
>
>4. **Insufficient Depth in Model Stability, Convergence, and Theoretical Analysis**
>
>   - **Issue Manifestation**

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-143.md

>     ：The article provides a mapping from second-order IIR to RNN when introducing the weight matrix of FRIRNN, but only briefly discusses the stability of RNN without offering theoretical guarantees or sufficient experimental validation. For example:
>
>     1. When the injected IIR parameters correspond to non-optimal or boundary instability, will the RNN experience gradient explosion or numerical instability during training?
>     2. For the spline activation function (B-spline), the article only mentions the ideas of odd symmetry and directional constraints but lacks quantitative analysis or appendix proofs of the activation function's convergence properties.
>
>   - **Suggestion**: Include more discussion on the stability and convergence of the network structure in the appendix or main text; it would be best to provide some numerical experiments to demonstrate the impact of different initial IIR parameter configurations on convergence.
>
>5. **The paper's structure and logical flow have some jumps and could be better organized**
>
>   - Issues:
>
>     :
>
>     1. Some concepts appear before they are explained, which slightly reduces readability. For instance, before introducing FRIRNN in Section 3, concepts like "relative transfer function" and "slice injection" already appear at the end of Section 2 without timely explanation.
>     2. There are many derivations in the appendix, but the main text also contains brief derivations; it is sometimes difficult to distinguish which should be in the main text and which should be detailed in the appendix.
>
>   - **Suggestion**: Provide brief explanations and references for key definitions (FRIRNN, KAN, physical constraint ideas for spline activation, etc.) when they first appear; for more detailed mathematical derivations, they can be presented in the appendix with concise summaries in the main text. This will help readers follow the "main thread" of the article more smoothly.
>
>6. **Improvements in charts and visualization details**
>
>   - Issues:
>
>     :
>
>     1. Labels or text in some illustrations are too small, affecting the reading experience.
>     2. Figures 1 and 2 (such as the physical diagram and schematic of the vibration table) could be redrawn or rearranged in subsequent versions to highlight the key structures and signal flows the article aims to convey.
>     3. It is recommended to add quantitative labels (units / dB / amplitude, etc.) to the axes of key figures (such as frequency response compensation effect diagrams and input-output curve comparison diagrams), rather than just showing qualitative curve trends.
>
>   - **Suggestion**: Improve the quality of all charts in the revised manuscript, especially for key results like "frequency response comparison before and after compensation." It would be best to provide numerical differences (e.g., peak drift, offset amplitude) or directly annotate key parameter changes in the figures to strengthen persuasiveness.
>
>7. **Writing style and language expression**
>
>   - **Issues**: The overall technical expression is fluent, but there are occasional issues with sentence structure coherence and unclear subject-verb agreement. It is recommended to polish the language before finalizing the manuscript to ensure accuracy and readability.
>   - **Suggestion**: If possible, collaborate with native English speakers or professional editing services for better results.
>
>------

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-144.md

>## IV. Are There Any Structural Fatal Flaws?
>
>- Conclusion
>
>  : No structural or directional fatal flaws were found.
>
>  - The direction of the article aligns with TIE's focus on the field of industrial electronics and sensors.
>  - The main issues lie in supplementing more complete experimental reproducibility, comparison and discussion with existing literature, details of theoretical analysis, and the organization of text and figures.
>  - If the authors can respond and revise each point, the article has the potential to meet the acceptance requirements.
>
>------
>
>## V. Summary
>
>In summary, the FRIKAN method proposed in this manuscript is relatively novel and has potential applications in the field of embedded sensor compensation and nonlinear processing. The article demonstrates a substantial amount of work in experimental data and model validation. The paper is relatively well-matched with the readership and topic direction of TIE. Given that there are still several issues mentioned above that need revision and improvement, the overall recommendation is: **Major Revision**, and the revised manuscript should particularly emphasize sufficient improvements in reproducibility, comparative experiments, and applicability to industrial scenarios. If the authors can adequately address these revision comments in the next draft, there is a good chance of acceptance by this journal. Wishing the research work smooth progress!
>
># January 16, 2025
>
>Hyperparameters have been supplemented, and a real pulse time-domain data still needs to be added (this also aligns with the previous plan).
>
>(Reviewing the initial draft according to the standards of SCI Q1 TIE, providing a judgment of rejection/major revision/minor revision/acceptance, and giving specific reasons. This article will be translated into English before publication, so the issue of Chinese-English mixing is not considered for now. Then, a judgment and detailed explanation are provided on whether the paper has any hard flaws/fatal structural defects, and the problems in the paper are explained in detail according to the severity of the issues. The images are the illustrations of the paper.)
>
>**Review Comments and Conclusion: Recommend "Major Revision" before considering acceptance**
>
>------
>
>The following comments are based on the common high standards of IEEE TIE (Transactions on Industrial Electronics) for papers, evaluating from aspects such as innovation, completeness, depth of experimental verification, writing, and formatting. The paper overall has a certain level of innovation, integrating physical priors with neural network methods to compensate for the nonlinear response of electrochemical seismometers (MET), which is a novel approach. The experiments cover multiple frequencies and amplitudes, demonstrating good engineering background value. However, the paper still requires significant revisions and supplements, and does not fully meet the strict review standards of SCI Q1 TIE. The following comments are listed in order of the severity of the issues.
>
>------
>
>### I. Main Issues in Structure and Experimental Design
>
>1. **The distinction from existing work needs to be clearer (Severity: High)**
>     Although the authors have cited methods such as PINNs, RVTDCNN, Volterra series, Wiener/NARMAX in the introduction and related work, the explanation of the principles, limitations of these traditional or recent methods, and the core differences with the proposed FRIKAN is still insufficient. The literature review section should further highlight:

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-145.md

>   - How does the existing literature differ from the approach of this study in addressing nonlinear compensation at the "frequency response level"?
>   - What are the **quantitative** or **theoretical** advantages of FRIKAN compared to physics-constrained/heuristic networks such as PINNs and RVTDCNN?
>   - In the research on nonlinear compensation for other sensors (e.g., piezoelectric sensors), are there any precedents for similar integration of frequency response information? If so, a detailed comparison is required; if not, the innovation should be emphasized even more.
>2. **Experimental validation is insufficient to prove universality for more complex excitations or multi-scenarios (severity: high)**
>     Most of the experiments in this paper focus on "pure sine wave sweep" conditions. Although sweep and amplitude scanning are necessary methods for studying the amplitude-frequency drift of sensors, they are not sufficient to demonstrate performance under real seismic waveforms (which usually contain multi-frequency components, random magnitude changes, etc.). It is recommended to supplement the "experiment" or "discussion" section with:
>   - Test validation under **more complex excitation scenarios** (e.g., random vibrations with multi-component superposition or short-duration pulse signals).
>   - If actual seismic environment testing is difficult, consider synthesizing more seismologically realistic composite waveforms on a vibration table to demonstrate FRIKAN's compensation effectiveness and generalization under random, multi-modal inputs.
>3. **Insufficient completeness and clarity in theoretical derivation (severity: medium)**
>     Although the appendix provides the derivation from a second-order IIR filter to FRIRNN, some key formulas are too abrupt; additionally, the paper claims that the B-spline activation function satisfies odd symmetry and co-directional monotonicity, but only provides a simple algorithm pseudocode. It is recommended to:
>   - Systematically and concisely present the "mathematical form" or "equivalent constraint conditions" derivation process for odd symmetry and co-directionality in the main text, and explain why it can represent the physical characteristics of MET.
>   - For the origin and development of FRIKAN's loss function (especially the amplitude-frequency loss), it is recommended to provide a clearer derivation context in the main text to facilitate reviewers' quick understanding of its physical motivation and the logic between formulas.
>4. **Lack of analysis on the model's sensitivity to noise and measurement errors (severity: medium)**
>     Sensors in actual testing often face uncertainties such as environmental noise, circuit noise, and mechanical coupling stray. Although the paper mentions that overfitting to high-frequency noise in the time domain should be avoided, there is no systematic "robustness" or "noise sensitivity" evaluation. It is recommended to:
>   - Consider whether FRIKAN compensation degrades under different signal-to-noise ratios (SNR).
>   - If possible, add artificial noise or additional interference in experiments to compare the compensation accuracy of FRIKAN with other models (e.g., LSTM, RVTDCNN) under noisy conditions.
>
>------
>
>### II. Issues in Writing and Formatting

## 翻译 private_upload\default_user\2025-01-26-14-53-12\README.md.part-146.md

>1. **Chart Readability and Illustration Consistency (Severity: Medium)**
>     Currently, the layout styles of Figures 1, 3, 4, 6, 7, and 8 are not uniform. Some are schematic diagrams, while others are experimental curves, with inconsistencies in fonts, labels, color descriptions, etc. Some symbols in the figures (such as η\etaη, \fn\fn\fn) sometimes do not match the main text. It is recommended to perform a unified layout and symbol check before finalizing the manuscript to ensure the clarity and consistency required for submission to TIE.
>2. **Language and Formatting Issues (Severity: Medium-Low)**
>     Submitting to an English journal requires the entire text to be in English. If multiple Chinese annotations or footnotes are retained in the English manuscript, ensure they are removed or uniformly translated in the final layout. Also, check the formula labels, reference citation style (should be consistent under IEEEtran), and ensure the fonts for physical quantities and subscripts are uniform throughout the text.
>3. **Timeliness and Diversity of References (Severity: Low)**
>     Although there are many references, attention should be paid to the latest developments in the past two to three years in high-level journals/conferences (such as IEEE TIE, TIM, IM, IFAC, Sensors, etc.) regarding sensor nonlinear compensation and small-sample physical information fusion. Consider adding more references for discussion.
>
>------
>
>### III. Are There Any Critical/Structural Flaws
>
>From the content framework and core ideas, the article does not have any irreparable "critical" flaws. The main structure (Introduction → Model → Experiment → Results) is relatively complete, and it provides theoretical derivations, experiments, and comparative results. The research approach is basically reasonable, and the experimental phenomena and conclusions are highly consistent, indicating that the method itself does not have obvious errors that violate physical laws or logic. Therefore, there are no structural flaws that would warrant direct rejection. However, to be formally accepted by TIE, further significant improvements are needed in experimental scenario expansion, theoretical completeness, and the interpretation of charts and text.
>
>------
>
>### Overall Recommendations
>
>Based on the above issues, it is recommended that the manuscript undergo **Major Revision**. The authors should focus on supplementing experimental validation under more complex excitation scenarios, further strengthening the comparison and explanation with existing literature, and improving the discussion on noise/uncertainty and model stability. If the revisions are thorough, the paper still has publication value in terms of innovation, interpretability, and practical performance on embedded platforms. We look forward to the authors making targeted revisions in the next version.

>The following content is a **simulated** review comment for the author's reference. This review comment covers the common review points and format requirements of the journal (IEEE Transactions on Industrial Electronics, SCI Q1), specifically including the overall evaluation of the manuscript, recommendation, reasons for modifications or supplements (listed in order of severity), whether there are structural fatal flaws, and whether key data figures that may lead to rejection are missing. Please modify or improve accordingly based on actual needs.
